     572             : 
     573             : /* Chooses which font to open from a TTC TrueType Collection font file.      */
     574             : /*                                                                           */
     575             : /* There are five ways that one enclosed font is selected:                   */
     576             : /*   1)  there is only one font enclosed, so we force defaulting to that one.*/
     577             : /*   2a) the filename has a font index appended, we choose that N'th font.   */
     578             : /*   2b) the filename has a font name appended, we try to match that name    */
     579             : /*           in list of discovered font names and select that named font.    */
     580             : /*   3)  the user is prompted with a list of all discovered font names, and  */
     581             : /*           asked to select one, and then that N'th font is chosen.         */
     582             : /*   4)  when there is no UI, then font index zero is used.                  */
     583             : /*                                                                           */
     584             : /* On failure and no font is chosen, returns false.                          */
     585             : /*                                                                           */
     586             : /* On success, true is returned.  The chosen font name (allocated) pointer   */
     587             : /*   is returned via 'chosenname'. Additionally, the file position is set    */
     588             : /*   pointing to the chosen TTF font offset table, ready for reading the     */
     589             : /*   TTF header.                                                             */
     590             : /*                                                                           */
     591             : /* Example filename strings with appended font selector:                     */
     592             : /*     ./tests/fonts/mingliu.windows.ttc(PMingLiU)                           */
     593             : /*     ./tests/fonts/mingliu.windows.ttc(1)                                  */
     594             : /*                                                                           */
     595             : /* 'offsets' is a list of file offsets to each enclosed TTF offset table.    */
     596             : /* 'names' is a list of font names as found in each enclosed name table.     */
     597             : /* 'names' is used to search for a matching font name, or to present as a    */
     598             : /*    list to the user via ff_choose() to select from.                       */
     599             : /*  Once the chosen font index is determined, offsets[choice] is used to     */
     600             : /*    call fseek() to position to the chosen TTF header offset table. Then   */
     601             : /*    the chosen font name is copied into 'chosenname'.                      */
     602             :

    1256          34 : static void readdate(FILE *ttf,struct ttfinfo *info,int ismod) {
    1257             :     int i, date[4];
    1258             :     /* TTFs have creation and modification timestamps in the 'head' table.  */
    1259             :     /* These are 64 bit values in network order / big-endian and denoted    */
    1260             :     /* as 'LONGDATETIME'.                                                   */
    1261             :     /* These timestamps are in "number of seconds since 00:00 1904-01-01",  */
    1262             :     /* noted some places as a Mac OS epoch time value.  We use Unix epoch   */
    1263             :     /* timestamps which are "number of seconds since 00:00 1970-01-01".     */
    1264             :     /* The difference between these two epoch values is a constant number   */ 
    1265             :     /* of seconds, and so we convert from Mac to Unix time by simple        */
    1266             :     /* subtraction of that constant difference.                             */
    1267             : 
    1268             :     /*      (31781 * 65536) + 45184 = 2082844800 secs is 24107 days */
    1269          34 :     int date1970[4] = {45184, 31781, 0, 0}; 
    1270             : 
    1271             :     /* As there was not (nor still is?) a portable way to do 64-bit math aka*/
    1272             :     /* "long long" the code below works on 16-bit slices of the full value. */
    1273             :     /* The lowest 16 bits is operated on, then the next 16 bits, and so on. */
    1274             : 
    1275          34 :     date[3] = getushort(ttf);
    1276          34 :     date[2] = getushort(ttf);
    1277          34 :     date[1] = getushort(ttf);
    1278          34 :     date[0] = getushort(ttf);
    1279             : 
    1280         136 :     for ( i=0; i<3; ++i ) {
    1281         102 :         date[i] -= date1970[i];
    1282         102 :         date[i+1] += date[i]>>16;
